Yu Hengqiu's Audacious Actions: Impersonating a Military Officer to Defraud People of Property, Captured by Haiheng Ship Crew 167

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiheng ship, returning to Shanghai from Shantou and Guangzhou this time, discovered a fraudster named Yu Hengqiu impersonating a military officer upon arrival in Shanghai. A large number of forged official documents and seals of the Ministry of Military Affairs, Chiang Kai-shek's personal seal, and various symbols were seized. He has been handed over to the Water Police Station and will be sent to court for interrogation. The details of this incident are as follows:

Impersonating a Military Officer: On the 27th of last month, the Haiheng ship sailed from Shanghai to Shantou and Guangzhou for the seventh time. At that time, a young military officer boarded the ship wearing a uniform and the insignia of Yu Jian, Section Chief of the First Section of the Ordnance Department of the Army Ministry. When boarding the ship, he purchased a second-class ticket, requesting a half-price ticket in the name of a military officer. After boarding the ship, he was very close to the crew. According to him, he was ordered by the Central Government to go to Guangdong to collect a large sum of money from Chen Jitang. He claimed that he had been selected by the Ministry of Military Affairs to study ordnance abroad, and the tuition fee of 40,000 yuan had been approved by the three ministries of military affairs, foreign affairs, and industry, with 15,000 yuan allocated by the Central Government and the remaining 25,000 yuan to be supplemented by Chen Jitang of Guangdong. Chen Jitang had already agreed to pay, and he was going to collect this large sum of money. He then took out a training order for 40,000 yuan of tuition fees jointly issued by the three ministries of military affairs, foreign affairs, and industry, as well as a passport for Yu Jian, Section Chief of the First Section of the Ordnance Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs, and a certificate of scholarship for students in the United States issued by the Central Government. The crew did not know it was fake and believed it to be true, showing great respect for Yu Jian.

Scamming Money on the Ship: Yu Jian was a young and promising man, eloquent, and a good writer. He got along well with the crew on the Haiheng ship. Yu's intentions were deep. He first gave small gifts to people to get close. There were also frequent banquets between the crew and passengers on the ship. Three of the crew members, Zheng, Su, and Li, often chatted with Yu Jian. Unexpectedly, Yu Jian took an inch and wanted a mile, using this opportunity to cheat people out of money. He said that he was going to Guangdong to collect a large sum of money for his scholarship, but he had to leave Beijing in a hurry and did not bring much travel money. He asked to borrow some money from each of them temporarily, and once he received 25,000 yuan, he would return it. The crew did not suspect that he was deceiving them. Zheng lent him 89 yuan, and Li lent him 10 yuan.

Scamming in Shanghai: In five or six days on the ship, Yu learned the history of each crew member. He even inadvertently learned the addresses of Zheng and Su's family members and the situation of their relatives and friends. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Guangdong, Yu disappeared from the Haiheng and returned to Shanghai on another ship. He then impersonated Su and Zheng to swindle money from their relatives and friends such as Hu Yumo. At the same time, he used the crew members' business cards to swindle and deceive outside. The Haiheng crew members did not know it at first. Later, they received inquiries from their relatives and friends and realized that Yu was a con artist. They immediately telegraphed Shanghai to inform their family members not to be fooled. Some of the crew members also sent someone on the Taikoo ship to return to Shanghai to investigate the matter.

Walking Right Into the Net: At 3:00 PM on the 24th, the Haiheng ship returned to Shanghai from Nanhua. As soon as the ship docked at the Nan Dock, the con artist Yu Jian, impersonating a military officer, was found lurking at the Jinliyuan Dock. The Haiheng ship's escort team discovered him and reported to the captain. They immediately captured the con artist at the dock, temporarily placed him in the fifth-class cabin, and assigned several security police to guard him. The scammed crew members Zheng, Su, Li, etc. questioned him about impersonating them and defrauding them. Yu lowered his head and said nothing, admitting that he had done this out of economic pressure. Because it was Sunday and the China Merchants Bureau was closed, he was guarded in the ship overnight. During this time, he was ordered to hand over all the items used to cheat people out of money. Yu then went to the Tonghe Public Inn in the French Concession and took out all the items.

Evidence Seized: The most important items handed over by the con artist included: (1) A passport for Yu Jian, Section Chief of the First Section of the Ordnance Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs; (2) A certificate of scholarship for students in the United States; (3) A document from the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government; (4) An order from the Executive Yuan; (4) An order for the Education Section Education Fund (salary of 600 yuan); (5) An order from the three ministries of military affairs, industry, and foreign affairs of the National Government (to collect 25,000 yuan in tuition fees in Guangdong); (6) The insignia of Qu Yong, Professor of Civil Engineering of the Ordnance Department of the Army Ministry; (7) The insignia of Yu Jian, Section Chief of the Ministry of Military Affairs; (8) A sign for Chen Jiaduo, Commander of the Fujian Provincial Garrison; (9) A sign for Qu Peiduo, Secretary of the Fourth Army Group; (10) A sign for Qu Peicheng, Professor of Engineering of the Training Corps of the First Army Group; (11) Four blank three-star insignias; (12) Qu Yong's passport for going abroad; (13) A magnetic badge of Chiang Kai-shek; (13) A pair of colonel's collar badges; (14) A seal of the Ministry of Military Affairs (wood carving), a seal of Minister He; (15) A small wooden seal of Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government; (16) A seal of He Jian, and five other wooden seals of various types; (10) (7) A star insignia of the U.S. Consul; (18) A box of lead type; a bundle of other miscellaneous documents; and a fake diamond ring, and three pawn tickets.

Confession: In the ship, Yu Jian wrote a confession, stating: "Yu Jian, real name Hengqiu, 23 years old, from Xiangyin, Hunan, graduated from Dalou Middle School, father is 60 years old, mother is 50 years old, grandmother is 80 years old. Came to Beijing in February 1934 to seek employment. A friend introduced him to be a secretary in the 16th Army. He was unable to cope in less than two months due to contracting gonorrhea. He returned to Beijing after a month and had no way out. He had no food to eat and no clothes to wear. Therefore, he borrowed 200 yuan from the secretary of the escort team, which he has not yet repaid. He returned to Beijing and stayed at the Zhengda Hotel in Dapingqiao, owing a lot of money and unable to return to Beijing. Therefore, this January, he went to Guangdong again on the Haiheng, intending to get travel money to return to Beijing. When he arrived in Guangdong, he had no money because his cousin's store had moved from the fourth shop to the public welfare store, so he could not go. He returned to Shanghai on the Haiheng, again without a penny. He deliberately intended to get money to return to Beijing. He originally wanted to become sworn brothers with Zheng, and took a photo together, and borrowed 89 yuan from him. He also swindled 10 yuan from Li, and forged the seals of Minister He, Mr. Zheng, the Chinese Consulate in the United States, and Qu Xiangheng and Qu Litao, as well as an official document from the Ministry of Military Affairs. He came to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday and was discovered by the crew of the Haiheng. I hope you will have compassion and mercy, and forgive the ignorance of youth. From now on, I will correct my mistakes and make a new start. My actions this time were really to get money to live on, and there was no other purpose. I now regret it and am willing to return home, and I will never again borrow the name of others to swindle outside. If I do so again, I am willing to be punished by law, etc." (Omitted below)

Sent to the Water Police: The crew members of the Haiheng had previously telegraphed Beijing to inquire about whether there was such a person as Yu Jian in the Ministry of Military Affairs. They received a reply that there was indeed such a person as Yu Jian in the Ordnance Department, but he was over 50 years old and had not left Beijing. It was obvious that he was an impostor. Yesterday, the Haiheng affairs director reported to the General Bureau as usual, and the bureau sent Shi Weijun to the ship. At the same time, the Jianghai Customs Water Police Station was notified. At 1:30 PM, the Water Police Station sent criminal department leader Huang Zhenlin to the Haiheng ship to take away the con artist Yu Jian and the private forged official documents and seals.

Hu Yizang's "The Raising of Goldfish" Published, Available at The Commercial Press 170

Recently, the trend of raising goldfish has become increasingly popular in countries around the world. However, if raised improperly, they are easily killed. Mr. Hu Yizang has compiled the book "The Raising of Goldfish" based on ten years of breeding experience and referring to the experiences of breeders in the East and West. It has been published by The Commercial Press, priced at 35 cents per copy. The book covers the types of goldfish, methods of raising fry, types of feeding, points to distinguish between males and females, precautions for changing and filling water, secrets of artificial color change, signs of spawning, treatment of various diseases, protection from enemies, and the relationship between goldfish and aquatic plants. It is a comprehensive work unprecedented in China and a guide for goldfish enthusiasts. It is heard that Mr. Hu is now working on a sequel.

Zhu Jianqiu's Tragic Death Case Adjourned: Yesterday, Witnesses Described What They Knew of the Incident; The Official Adjourned the Trial, and the Verdict is Scheduled to Be Announced on the 30th Afternoon 173

The household registration section of the Zhenru Police Station, while investigating household registrations, caused Zhu Jianqiu, the owner of a family food store, to suffer torture at the hands of the police, with a large amount of water poured into his nose, resulting in suffocation and death. After forensic examination by the Research Institute, the prosecutor of the District Court, Lei Binzhang, repeatedly summoned witnesses and concluded the investigation. The chief of the police station, Zhou Pingyuan, officers Xing Guonong, chief Zhang Zhizhong, police officers Liu Mingqi, Ma Xiantu, and others were prosecuted for the crime of causing death by injury and brought to the criminal court, where Judge Shao Qinzhi conducted two public trials. Zhou Pingyuan and Xing Guonong tried to shirk responsibility, and their statements contradicted each other. By order, Zhou and Xing were separately detained, while Zhang Zhizhong and others were released on bail. The examining judge, for the sake of caution, repeatedly summoned witnesses for further questioning, as reported in previous issues. It is now learned that Zhou Pingyuan was previously released on bail by the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Shao held another court session to continue the trial. On the plaintiff's side, the deceased's younger brother, Zhu Shiying, and his private prosecution lawyer, Yan Hongxi, appeared in court. The defendants were represented by three lawyers, Lin Dawen, Feng Meixue, and Huang Shaochang. The Public Security Bureau sent police to escort Zhou Pingyuan to court. After the judge took his seat, he ordered the incarcerated Xing Guonong to be brought before the court. After a brief interrogation, the judge ordered the witness Yang Maorong to be brought before the court. According to Yang's testimony, he is 56 years old, from Changsha, Hunan, an employee of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, residing in Lujiabang, and related to Zhu Jianqiu as an uncle. The judge asked about what he said during the investigation, saying that although there was no signed statement at the time, there was a written record, and that today, before speaking in court, he must first sign a statement before speaking again. He was then asked to describe in detail the facts he knew. Yang replied that on the 25th, his nephew Zhu Shiying called to tell him that because of a mistake in the household registration, his apprentice had been detained by the police station and asked for help. At that time, he told his nephew that such minor matters would only result in a small fine. The next day (the 26th), Shiying called again, saying that the police station had sent six police officers to arrest his brother Jianqiu for a minor violation, which was truly muddled. After receiving the call, he replied that if it was so muddled, he would not interfere. On the morning of the 27th, Shiying personally came to his place and said that his brother Jianqiu had been fatally injured by torture in the police station. Hearing this, he immediately instructed Shiying to hire a lawyer to file a lawsuit in court and handle the matter according to law. The judge asked if he had asked Li Yunsheng of Lane Li Yunsheng to help his nephew resolve the household registration issue. Yang replied that he did, because after receiving the call from his nephew, he did not know anyone at the Zhenru Police Station, so he asked Li Yunsheng to help his nephew with the violation and instructed him to handle it according to the regulations. Next, the witness Li Yunsheng testified that he is 37 years old, from Nanchang, Jiangxi, and works in the Inspectorate of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The judge asked if he had made a preliminary report regarding the case, and that was why he had been summoned to court today. He was asked to state the facts as he knew them and that he must first sign a statement before speaking. The judge asked if he knew anyone at the Zhenru Police Station. Li replied that he only knew Inspector Lin. The judge asked him to state the facts he knew. Li replied that on the 25th, Yang Maorong asked him to help his nephew, who was detained at the Zhenru Police Station for a discrepancy in household registration. He asked him to go there and handle it according to the regulations. Upon receiving Yang Maorong's request, he informed Inspector Lin of the situation by phone. Lin replied that he would wait for the chief of the police station to return before making a decision. The judge asked if Inspector Lin had come to his place because Zhu Jianqiu's mother had made a scene at the police station and asked him to convey to Yang Maorong to persuade Zhu's mother to return home. Li replied that this was not the case. The judge then said to Yang Maorong, "What exactly do you mean by the word 'muddled' in your phone call?" Yang replied that on the 25th, his nephew called to ask for help, and on the 26th, he said that the police station was handling things in a muddled way, but his nephew was not mentally confused. As for Zhu Jianqiu's minor violation of household registration regulations, the Zhenru Police Station actually sent six police officers to arrest him. If there were ten or a hundred households with errors, would the entire police force have to go? However, his nephew's death was a small matter, but for the sake of the citizens in the future, he had to expose the inside story to serve as a warning for the future. Next, the witness Hong Xingchi testified that he is 23 years old, from Anhui, and a student at Southeast Medical College. At 6:00 PM on the 25th, five of them were eating dinner at Zhu Jianqiu's store. He saw that Zhu was full of energy and was cooking for them. After they finished eating, they chatted and dispersed. The next day at noon, they went back for lunch. According to the apprentice in the store, the store owner had gone to the police station for household registration matters, so no one was cooking. Since they had no food to eat, the five of them went to visit. On the way, they saw Zhu Jianqiu lying on a rickshaw, his face pale, his eyes frequently rolling upwards, and his throat swollen. Seeing this situation, they were deeply shocked. They asked why he was in this state, but Zhu could not speak. When they took off his clothes, they saw injuries on his back. They asked Zhu Jianqiu if he had been beaten at the police station, and Zhu nodded frequently. So they accompanied Zhu Jianqiu in the rickshaw back to the police station to question them. The police station denied beating him and said that there was a discrepancy in household registration and a fine of one yuan should be paid. So they paid one yuan on behalf of Zhu, and the police station issued a receipt. Seeing that Zhu Jianqiu's complexion was abnormal, they quickly ordered the rickshaw driver to take him to Southeast Hospital for treatment. The testimonies of Zhan Jihan, Hu Weisan, Yu Zheshen, and others were largely consistent with that of Hong Xingchi. Zhu Shiying testified that he called his uncle on the 25th to ask for help, and on the 26th, he called to tell him that the Zhenru Police Station was handling things in a muddled way. On the 27th, he went to his uncle's house to tell him the tragic death of his brother Jianqiu. At this point, the judge invited Prosecutor Lei Binzhang to court to present his case, stating that the facts of the case were extremely clear and that he should request a public judgment according to law. The defendants' lawyers, Lin Dawen and others, then rose to defend the defendants, stating that "There are strange things under the heavens. Just like the recent case of Ruan Lingyu's suicide by taking sleeping pills, the facts of why she committed suicide are being investigated. In this case, it cannot be proven who the perpetrator was. Moreover, the deceased went to another place after leaving the police station before going to the hospital. The court should carefully examine this. The prosecutor's indictment is based entirely on speculation. They request that a verdict of not guilty be announced." Finally, private prosecution lawyer Yan Hongxi stated that "Police torture in police stations is a public secret. However, the chief and officers would not directly pour water. If police officers inflict torture, they must have received orders from the chief and officers. Now, I request that the private prosecution investigate. The victim Zhu Jianqiu was 39 years old. Counting to 60 years old, there are still 21 years. Calculating at 100 yuan per month, I request 25,200 yuan. The cost of clothing and coffin is 303 yuan, totaling 25,503 yuan, for which all defendants are jointly liable." The judge then asked Zhou Pingyuan and others if they had any final statements and how they would respond to the private prosecution. Zhou and the others replied that they did not commit the assault and did not want to pay compensation. Zhou Pingyuan also stated that Zhu Jianqiu was in the police station for four hours and that he never saw him. As for the statement that "two people helped him out of the police station," he only heard it from others. The judge, having heard the testimony, considered the trial concluded and scheduled the verdict to be announced at 2:00 PM on the 30th of this month. Xing Guonong was returned to custody, and Zhou Pingyuan was taken back by police from the Public Security Bureau. Attorney Yan rose and requested that the court detain Zhou, as Zhou had already been dismissed from his post and there was a risk of escape. The judge said that Zhou Pingyuan was released on bail by the Public Security Bureau and that there should be no other concerns. He then adjourned the court. By that time, all the houses were lit up.

Special Article

Jin Cheng Bank 23rd Year Business Report (13) 181

Corresponding to the interbank lending market is the securities market. When productive enterprises prosper and interbank lending rates are high, the stock market declines. When productive enterprises decline, investors shift their attention to bonds, causing bond prices to rise. According to Table 3, the Shanghai bond index shows that bond prices from January to June were 19% higher. In July, they reached a peak of 111.9, 31.93% higher than the average at the beginning of the year. Although they gradually fell after August, the year-end figure of 98.9 was still more than 18% higher than at the beginning of the year. The annual average was 96.73, 24.76% higher than in the 20th year of the Republic. In terms of transaction volume, this year was over 400 million yuan, an increase of over 78.4 million yuan or 19.6% compared to the 22nd year of the Republic. The decline in industry and commerce can be seen from this. The amount of bill exchange and public bill collection also indicates the volume of market transactions. The first four months of this year were quite sluggish, with a daily average of just over 40 million yuan. From May onwards, it gradually increased, and by December, the daily average was over 60 million yuan. However, this is still one-third lower than the daily average of 89.312 thousand yuan for public bill collection in the same period of the 20th year of the Republic. The annual daily average was 53 million yuan, which is also inferior to the annual daily average of 75 million yuan in the 20th year of the Republic. However, it is an increase of 7.6 million yuan compared to the annual average of the 22nd year of the Republic. In terms of clearing institutions, the bill exchange office accounted for an annual average of 20.1%, approximately twice the annual average of 11.6% in the 22nd year of the Republic. Money shop public bills accounted for 79.9% this year (see Table 3 for monthly details of the daily average amount). (To be continued)

A Memorable Scene from the Coal Mine Basketball Game: Jinan Defeats Fudan and Seizes the Championship, Resulting in 51 to 40; Central Wins Against Chih Chih in Another Match 184

The Jiangnan University Basketball Championship has been underway since its commencement, with more than half of the games completed. Yesterday, there were two matches: Jinan versus Fudan, and Central versus Chih Chih, held at Jiangwan and Shuidian Road, respectively. Jinan and Fudan are known for their strong teams. Since the beginning of the competition, neither team has suffered a defeat, truly making them two giants in this year's league. Therefore, yesterday's match was nothing short of a championship final. As a result, Jinan, relying on the bravery of its five key players, defeated Fudan with a score of 51 to 40. The Jiangnan University Championship will inevitably move from Jiangwan to Zhenru. (Last year's champion was Fudan.) With Jinan defeating Fudan, all other matches should be easily won. In another match, Central narrowly defeated Chih Chih with a score of 24 to 21.

Jinan Crushes Fudan

The Gymnasium is Packed

The match between Jinan and Fudan took place at 3:30 PM yesterday afternoon in Fudan's Jiangwan Gymnasium. Since the outcome of this match was related to winning the championship, students from both Jinan and Fudan, deeply devoted to their schools, were willing to sacrifice their studies to watch the game. It was as if they were thinking, "Classes can be skipped, but this match is a must-see." Therefore, around 3 o'clock, the gymnasium was already packed like sardines. The entrances and exits were also blocked by the audience, cutting off traffic. Those who arrived later had to stand outside the door, quietly listening to the shouts from within.

Jinan Crushes from the Start

When the two teams met, Gui Ren added the finishing touch, and the scoreboard displayed eight points. Fudan relied on Fu Xiangrui to score a point from a free throw. Jinan's Xu Heng was not one to be outdone, adding two points, making it 12 to 1. Fudan's Weng Zhou and Fu combined their throws and free throws, rapidly increasing the score by 14 points, making it 16 to 15, trailing by one point. Before long, Fudan's Weng Renan scored a point from a free throw, tying the score at 16 to 16. As they faced off, Jinan's players scored 14 points in one breath, making it 30 to 16, leading again. Fudan's Zhou Dayun scored two baskets from the middle, making the score 30 to 20. The first half ended there.

Fudan's Counterattack Ultimately Suffers Defeat

As the second half began, Fudan's players remained extremely calm in this unfavorable environment, constantly thinking of ways to win unexpectedly. However, their opponent's defense was impenetrable, leaving them helpless. Jinan fought with increasing courage. The two players, Yin and Xu, made every shot. Fudan desperately chased after them, but the losses outweighed the gains. At this moment, the score became 39 to 27. About fifteen minutes in, Jinan's Xu Heng committed his fourth foul and was ejected from the game. Although Fudan also seized the opportunity to counterattack, Jinan's luck with the ball was prosperous, and every shot they took hit the mark. As a result, Jinan won with a score of 51 to 40.

Publication of Chinese Wrestling Method 189

Mr. Tong Zhongyi, a famous martial arts master, excels in combat techniques and injury treatment, and has particularly extensive experience in wrestling. Recently, he compiled his decades of teaching experience into a book titled "Chinese Wrestling Method." It covers the basic exercises of wrestling, the implementation of techniques, and uses illustrations to explain in detail. The book is finely printed on beige coated paper, with over three hundred copperplate illustrations. Even those who have not learned martial arts can follow the illustrations and teach themselves without a teacher. Those who wrote prefaces for the book include Zhang Zhijiang, Director of the Central Martial Arts Academy; Xiang Zongding, Director of the Qingdao Martial Arts Academy; and Liu Pixian of the Henan Martial Arts Academy. Military and political leaders such as Liu Xiang, Chairman of Sichuan Province, and Chu Minyi of the Executive Yuan, as well as Mayor Wu Pan Gongzhan of this city, all wrote inscriptions and prefaces, considering it a rare find among martial arts books. At a time when the New Life Movement is being vigorously promoted, physical training is particularly urgent. Moreover, wrestling is not only a unique and clever technique for self-defense, but also has a significant effect on cultivating the spirit of perseverance and struggle, and is also an extremely interesting sport. The book is published by the Chinese Wrestling Society and is available for sale at the National Martial Arts Hall at Xin Kaihe City, Minquan Road, at the Dafang Art Company on the 4th floor of 692 Niuzhuang Road, Zhejiang Road, and at Qixin Bookstore and Xiaojingshanfang in this city, as well as at martial arts schools in various provinces and cities in other areas.

Private Vocational School Subsidy Fees: Application Forms Must Be Submitted to the Ministry by the End of Next Month 191

(Nanjing, 25th) The Ministry of Education issued an order to private vocational schools and above, stating that the application for subsidies for private vocational schools and above, is based on Article 5 of the "Outline of the Distribution Method of Subsidies for Private Vocational Schools and Above" in the current "Issuance of Subsidy Fees for Private Vocational Schools and Above," which stipulates that "Private vocational schools and above that apply for subsidies must submit an application form for subsidies, fill it out accurately according to the items formulated by the Ministry of Education, and submit it to the Ministry of Education before the end of April each year." All schools that meet the conditions stipulated in Article 2 of the Outline, and wish to apply for subsidies for equipment fees or special chair fees for the 24th year, must accurately submit the application form before the end of April in accordance with the regulations, for review and approval.

National Reading Competition Organized by the Chinese Cultural Construction Association; A Bonus of 3,000 Yuan to Encourage Scholarly People; Registration from April 25th to the End of April 192

In order to create a national atmosphere of learning and improve cultural standards, the Chinese Cultural Construction Association has specially organized a National Reading Competition, with registration offices in the provincial and municipal branches of the Cultural Construction Association. Registration began on April 25th. The first reading period is from April 1st to the end of September. Those with excellent results will be awarded a bonus of 3,000 yuan to encourage them. The declaration and registration methods are recorded as follows:

Declaration: "Living in this era of severe national crisis, in terms of the nation-state, we must strengthen our national strength, which goes without saying. However, the formation of a country is based on the growth of its people, so to strengthen national strength, we must first strengthen the abilities of our people. Moreover, in this era of fierce international competition, what determines victory or defeat is the actual strength of politics, economy, and military, but the foundation lies entirely in the intelligence of the people. Because what is called politics and economy is nothing more than a total manifestation of the people's intelligence, therefore, only a people with high intelligence can ensure their existence and not be wiped out by others. In the past, China, although repeatedly conquered by foreign races, was able to maintain its independent status and cause the militarily victorious race to be assimilated by us. The reason for this is that our country's people are more intelligent than the foreign races. However, now the times have changed, and our intelligence, undeniably, is far inferior to that of European, American, and Japanese countries. Therefore, not only is our science backward, but also our political and economic strength is far inferior to theirs. Therefore, at this time, the strengthening of national intelligence is essential, and the only way to strengthen national intelligence is for the whole country to devote themselves to hard work and engage in reading and research. This is the primary significance of the Chinese Cultural Construction Association launching the Reading Competition on its anniversary.

Moreover, in terms of individuals, such as the preparation of life skills and the understanding of social customs, all depend on reading. As the saying goes, reading clarifies principles. And at this time of economic difficulty and difficult livelihoods, reading to seek knowledge seems even more necessary. However, the reality is exactly the opposite. What permeates society is an atmosphere of not reading. Depravity, languor, idleness, and debauchery have become fashionable. Not only do young students make it a common practice to make trouble, but also the literary world values humor and light essays. Because of this, the air of falsehood infects people, creating a frivolous and clamorous atmosphere. To reform this habit, we naturally have to start from the practical aspects, so that everyone knows the importance of learning. This transformation from a style of enjoyment and decadence to a style of hard work and refinement is the secondary significance of the Chinese Cultural Construction Association launching the Reading Competition.

Third, the biggest shortcoming of today's school system is that it uses money as a ladder to higher education. Poor children, even if they have talent, often suffer from a lack of opportunities to enter school. Secondly, all the lessons are often unnecessarily prolonged. There are often courses that can be completed in a few months, but must be studied for a year. This is a painful experience for young people with superior talent who cannot develop. The intention of launching the Reading Competition is to correct this shortcoming. First, to provide assistance for poor children to rise, and second, to provide opportunities for young people who are eager to learn to study and improve themselves. Therefore, on the one hand, we are negotiating with publishing bookstores to sell textbooks and books at the lowest possible price, and on the other hand, we are offering bonuses as encouragement.

In short, the purpose of the Reading Competition is nothing more than what is stated in the outline: to encourage reading, cultivate a good atmosphere of learning, and improve cultural standards. But this is the basic work of building Chinese culture and revitalizing the Chinese nation. We hope that all seniors and talents at home and abroad will not hesitate to help. Much obliged."

The Fourth Guidance District of Anhui Holds a Local Education Guidance Conference, Resolving 23 Proposals to Improve Local Education 193

(Dispatch from Xuancheng) The Anhui Provincial Department of Education, in order to actively promote local education and to integrate normal school education with local education, has implemented a local education guidance system. The province is divided into six guidance districts, with each district using a provincial normal school as the guidance center. A district guidance committee is organized, with the principal of the normal school appointed by the Department of Education as the chairman. Each district also has a local education supervisor who is supervised and guided by the chairman and is responsible for guidance work. The Provincial Xuancheng Normal School is the central organ of the Fourth Guidance District, which encompasses eleven counties: Wuhu, Xuancheng, He County, Nanling, Fanchang, Hanshan, Jing County, Guangde, Langxi, Ningguo, and Dangtu. On the 15th of this month, Hu Jiajian, the principal of the Provincial Xuancheng Normal School and chairman of the district guidance committee, convened the first local education guidance conference at the Provincial Xuancheng Normal School. Those in attendance included educational administrative leaders, county supervisors, and representatives of educational service personnel from the eleven counties under its jurisdiction. Principal Hu Jiajian of Xuancheng Normal School presided over the meeting, which lasted three days and resolved twenty-three key proposals. These proposals covered promoting universal education, improving teaching methods, compiling and printing guidance publications, implementing communication research, organizing local education research associations, and preparing for summer primary school teacher training workshops. All these matters were discussed extensively, and concrete plans were formulated. The full text of the key resolutions of the conference is recorded below:

Educational Research Group: (1) Proposal to conduct local education communication research; (2) Educational administrative organs in each county within this district must urge primary schools in their respective counties to earnestly fill out the survey forms issued by the guidance committee, normal schools, or affiliated primary schools, so as to facilitate research and publication; (3) Proposal that the district guidance committee compile and distribute teaching processes and examples for each subject to primary schools within the district for teaching reference; (4) Proposal to edit and publish local education guidance publications for the district; (5) Proposal to revise arithmetic textbooks suitable for rural primary schools and people's schools; (6) Proposal to implement the baojia system in primary school student self-government organizations; (7) Before the entire guidance plan is finalized, the first phase of guidance in this district should pay special attention to the guidance of multi-grade and single-grade teaching; (8) Guidance matters in this district should focus on the implementation of production education, health education, and national defense education, with particular attention to multi-grade and single-grade teaching; (9) Proposal to organize a local education research association in the district; (10) The district education supervisor should assist each county in compiling local teaching materials; (11) Implementation plan for primary school labor practice; (12) Implementation plan for primary school civic training.

Educational Administration Group: (1) Request the Department of Education to issue a circular to all counties to establish short-term primary schools, simple primary schools, or two-part systems as much as possible to meet social needs; (2) Primary school teachers in each county should employ normal school graduates as much as possible and effectively protect their rights; (3) Proposal to organize universal education promotion associations in each county; (4) Rural primary schools and people's schools in each county in this district should coordinate with local baojia chiefs to pay attention to hygiene facilities; (5) Rigorously train normal school students; (6) Each county should designate more complete primary schools as central primary schools, delineate guidance areas, implement mobile guidance, and add a supervisor to be solely responsible for guidance; (7) How should the work of district education committee guidance be regulated; (8) District supervisors, county supervisors, and district education committees should communicate with each other to facilitate the implementation of the district guidance system; (9) How to stabilize the profession and life of primary school teachers; Teacher Training Group: (1) Seek further education for local education service personnel; (2) Propose a minimum reference book list for primary school teachers. Concrete measures have been formulated for each of the above resolutions. Among them, the proposal to organize a local education research association was submitted by the Provincial Xuancheng Normal School and was approved by the general assembly. In addition to organizational methods, the content of the proposal also details the research scope and objectives, which can not only serve as a basis for local education personnel in this district to study local education problems, but also be used as a reference for other districts. In addition, the proposals on universal education and teacher training are also very well-written. Therefore, this first guidance conference of the guidance district was very fruitful, it is said.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets 196

— (Yan Ming)

People are good at talking about purpose. All their behaviors are to achieve a certain purpose. However, in the process of achieving their conscious "purpose," they never feel that there is a final purpose. The so-called final purpose is "death."

Seen from the perspective of this "death" purpose, all the "purposes" that people want to achieve can be said to be merely means to achieve the "death" "purpose"! A person wants to escape from suffering and enter the path of life, but they don't know that the path of life is just a segment in the path of death.

Except for slight differences in time, giving birth to a child is equivalent to the death of an adult (the reason why "old man" is not written here is that people often die in their youth or prime of life). As soon as a person is born, they don't need training, and everyone is a long-distance runner on the sports field, competing to win the "death" championship.

Tears 197

— Jiao Xin

Zeng Wenzhenggong's diary says: "Suppressing desires is as difficult as a man's tears." He meant that a man's tears are as difficult as suppressing desires. But Liu Xuande's marriage to Lady Sun was entirely due to tears; Zhuge Kongming also preserved his life by weeping like a spring at the memorial service for Zhou Lang in Chaisangkou; as for the relief of the siege of Wu by Chu in the Spring and Autumn period, it was entirely due to Shen Daifu weeping for seven days and seven nights against the Qin court wall, shedding many tears. So who says men won't shed tears?

Tears and snot are inseparable brothers, always together. In colloquial terms, it's said: "a handful of snot, a handful of tears"; in literary terms, it's said: "tears and snot mingled."

"The wax candle turns to ashes, and tears begin to dry," but in fact, the wax candle never shed tears? It was just that the author at the time was full of depression and used it as a metaphor; so later, the resentful women in spring boudoirs couldn't help but be emotionally affected by this uninspired wax candle, and added a lot of sorrow out of thin air.

In "Dream of the Red Chamber," it is said that Lin Daiyu's crying is to repay the debt of tears owed to Jia Baoyu. Then, are all the women in the world who cry well also repaying debts of tears? The word "debt" is originally a vulgar word, but adding the word "tear" makes it very fragrant and seductive.

Tears have a salty taste. According to physiologists, water accounts for 99% of tears, and salt and protein each account for slightly less than 0.5%. Its function is to moisten the eyeballs and wash away the dust in the eye sockets, not just to express joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness.

The Nightingale's Lament 198

— Wu Yafei

When I arrived in Wuxi, I visited several friends that day, but in the evening I returned to the hotel alone, closed the door and flipped through two pages of "An Introduction to Chinese Studies"; however, I felt very restless and really had no mood to read any further. So I burst out of the hotel door and strolled towards every street. Aimlessly, I wandered around, my eyes darting everywhere, conscious of the night scene here.

I wandered onto this lonely street like a ghost; it was already past eleven o'clock, so most of the shops were closed, and the surroundings were quiet, so desolate that ghosts could almost be caught; this small city had sunk into that quiet rest, waiting for dawn to arrive.

"...The moon is curved and shines on the street...Thinking of my hometown is so miserable...How many people have no clothes or food...How many people have no home to return to..."

In a pitch-black alley, there was a gradually approaching erhu sound, along with a sorrowful song, sung by a woman. But the tone trembled very badly, as if it were a ghost crying, making my hair stand on end! Each sentence and sound she sang pierced my heart like a sharp knife. I really couldn't bear to listen to it, nor did I have the courage to listen any further! I suddenly stood in the dark, wanting to avoid them, but looking through a dim street lamp, I saw them walking towards me. The pale yellow light shone on their faces. A man in his forties was playing the erhu, and a woman in her thirties was humming with her mouth puckered. Their faces were as green as cabbage leaves, and their eyes were filled with melancholy. The man's eyelids drooped, without a trace of spirit, and the woman looked like she was suffering from insomnia.

At this time, I was like an explorer who had encountered a beast and fled back, or like a soldier returning from a defeated battle, hurriedly fleeing back to the hotel. I walked into the room and fell on the bed. I dared not recall the scene just now. I felt like a triumphant returner from an unimaginable world.

Different Pursuits 199

Xiao Xi Tian 200

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 11: Night Talks of a Sad Life, Life Is Originally a Dream, Scattered Footprints, Wind and Rain Too Deceiving

Huanhua smiled again and said, please come over, I still have a few words to say to you, I don't want you to help me with money. Jia Duocai heard him say this, thinking that if he didn't go to his room, maybe he would run over. Therefore, he answered in his mouth and walked over to this room again. At this time, Yang Huanhua was not the same as before. His face was covered with powder, and his hair was combed smoothly. Seeing people come in, he greeted them with a smile, pulling at his clothes, seeming a bit embarrassed. In the past, seeing Yang Huanhua would evoke a sense of disgust in Jia Duocai. Seeing his pitiful appearance under the lamp now, he didn't hate him so much. Instead, he comforted him and said: Just now, consider it a dream, don't take it to heart. What else do you want to say? Huanhua sat on the bed, looking at him suspiciously from a distance, and said with a flirty smile: Can Mr. Jia sit for a while longer? I have a longer story to tell you, but I definitely don't want you to help me with any money. He stated this again, followed by a charming smile. Jia Duocai couldn't bear to refuse again, so he nodded and smiled: Speak, anyway, I have nothing to do tonight, I'll listen to you. Huanhua pulled at her clothes again, coughed slightly twice, and then said: Let me tell you the stories of two women first. The first one is from Anhui. Jia Duocai laughed and said: How did you think of the story of Anhui people in Xiaoxitian in Xi'an? Huanhua said: Because she is also wandering in Xi'an like me. She is an eighteen-year-old girl, with snow-white skin, an oval face, and jet-black hair. She often comes to Xiaoxitian, Mr. Jia may have seen her. Jia Duocai said: Is she wearing a dark green silk skirt? Huanhua said: That's right, it's her. Don't look at her like that, running to the hotel every day, she is a well-read lady. Jia Duocai gave a sigh and said: Why does she like to run to Xiaoxitian, I think she seems to be doing business! (166)

The Imperial Incense Drifting Record 201

— Originally Written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

After listening to this very implicit remark of Yi, I couldn't help but sigh secretly, but I still couldn't help but think it was very cruel to throw the cocoons containing the silkworm chrysalises that were not yet dead into boiling water. I raised a question to the Empress Dowager again.

"Why not cut open one end of the cocoon first, take out the silkworm pupae, and then throw it into boiling water?"

"That's not possible"! The Empress Dowager seemed to find my question ridiculously funny, but she was not annoyed and still answered very patiently: "The cocoon must never be broken, if it is broken, it cannot be reeled. If it could be broken, why wouldn't we wait for the pupae inside to turn into moths, and after they drilled out, take them to reel silk? Because the silk on the cocoons is very neat and continuous, it won't work if it's broken; and to pick out a silk thread from a cocoon, you have to soak it in boiling water. So this method cannot be changed...

"Besides, even if those silkworm pupae are not scalded to death, taking them out first, after a few days they will just die anyway!" She frankly and pointedly broke my unconscious pity.

The Empress Dowager really regarded silkworms as a way to relieve fatigue. Although she set aside such a large part of the house in the Summer Palace specifically for silkworm breeding, and spent a lot of money on preparing supplies, purchasing mulberry leaves, and also raised so many girls who did nothing all year round to take care of silkworm breeding; this capital is really not small. But she never sold the cocoons she obtained, always using them to reel silk herself; and the reeled silk was absolutely not sold, and she didn't see any great use for it, just storing them in skeins, or to satisfy her own temporary pleasure, then teaching another group of silk-making girls to dye those skeins of silk with various bright colors, and then collect them. This is nothing more than spending a few more dollars. (277)

Quick Sketch of Cichangli Restaurant 202

— Zhang Muliang

At lunchtime, all the offices dismissed almost simultaneously. The restaurants on both sides of Cichangli straightened up those hot meals and hot dishes, waiting for the office workers to come and patronize; then, the eating life of the office workers began.

Diners wriggled and surged in, and Cichangli immediately became densely populated; latecomers had already been encroached upon by early birds!

These are all regular customers, most of them eat guest meals, and the price is uniformly two jiao in small silver coins per guest. Humph, don't think that customers who eat two-jiao guest meals are stingy, in fact, they eat like lions opening their mouths; think about it, for two jiao in small silver coins, you can choose a mixed dish at will (expensive ones are of course exceptions), like stir-fried meat slices, stir-fried eel shreds, small white hooves, etc., you can choose at will; if people with good appetites can also get some rice for free when it's not enough, I think there is probably no such bargain in small restaurants?

Many diners shouted for "small white hooves! Small white hooves..." The Puxi landlady said worriedly: "Oh dear! So many people want to eat small white hooves, I'm really going to lose money"!

One diner said to the waiter: "Today, stir-fry fish tofu with chili for me, make it so it tastes good, understand"? Then another one said: "Hey! Quickly make a salty meat tofu soup, the tofu should be cooked thoroughly, the salty meat should be lean, and there should be plenty of oil..."

In this noisy sound, Zhang San wants to eat fish, Li Si wants to eat meat, and the waiters in several restaurants are driven to the point where they have nowhere to go by the diners, so some diners eat and leave without paying, and swagger away. For this reason, the waiters are generally suffering in silence, with unspeakable grievances!

When lunchtime is over, the diners all wriggle out of Cichangli and walk to their respective offices.

Short story

Brothers 203

— Zhu Xun

Wang Jiren and Wang Zhongren, brothers, went to court over a property division issue. The lawyers on both sides issued statements refuting each other based on reason, and the news of the trial was published and republished in newspapers, becoming a recent hot topic.

I knew the brothers Jiren and Zhongren twenty years ago. At that time, Jiren's father was still a partner in a money shop and had not been promoted to manager or transferred to the banking industry, so the Wang family's financial situation was not as splendid as it is in recent years.

When I met Jiren and the others, we were together in Mr. Li's private school. At that time, Jiren was only eight years old; with his exquisite figure and handsome face, our classmates all loved him very much. Zhongren was even younger, only about six years old; with a round head and a face that was so rosy and glowing, he looked like an apple. His silly appearance often made me laugh unintentionally.

The authority of the teacher in the private school was indeed as lofty as that of the emperors in the autocratic era. When the teacher's eyes were wide open and the ruler struck the table loudly, even the number one naughty child would be frightened like a condemned prisoner, trembling in fear! We were no exception in Mr. Li's private school.

I remember one day, Mr. Li was probably angry because of his wife, and his face was so stern that it was scary; coincidentally, Zhongren's homework that day was not memorized well. When he was reciting, he recited the first sentence and forgot the next sentence, and couldn't get it out. Mr. Li threw the book down again and again, asking Zhongren to read it and then recite it, but when he went up the second and third times, he was still frightened and couldn't get it out stutteringly. Mr. Li got angry, picked up the ruler, and slammed it on the table. But this sound didn't scare Zhongren into reciting the book, but instead, he let out a cry and was scared into crying.

This cry made Mr. Li's anger even greater. He grabbed Zhongren, who was standing blankly beside him, and struck Zhongren's hand repeatedly with the ruler. However, because of the teacher's beating, Zhongren cried even louder; and the teacher's ruler struck even harder. In the end, the ruler was like raindrops, densely hitting Zhongren's body and head. The poor Zhongren was like a lamb wailing under the whip, waiting to die.

However, now this pair of loving brothers are in endless lawsuits over the property issue. Thinking of this past event, a layer of bewilderment suddenly floated into my heart.

Grain: Bulls Exit the Flour and Wheat Markets Early – Rumors of Tax Increase on Imported Wheat Surface in the Afternoon 212

After the flour market opened in the morning, prices for all months fell uniformly. Imported wheat quotations: Chicago down about 45 points, Canada down about 23 points. When prices opened, the decline in imported wheat was quite sharp. Coupled with the easing tensions in Eastern Europe, the previous weekend's surge was based solely on international changes. Now, there's an unsubstantiated rumor, so it's not credible. Therefore, sentiment was already weak when prices opened. Soon, bulls exited positions and factories offered supplies, with near-term down by a small fraction and distant-term down by two or three fractions. When prices opened in the afternoon, market sentiment gradually improved. Although large and small factories continued to sell, outside buyers were superstitious about a tax increase on imported wheat, so they were keen to buy. The near-term was also tightening for spot flour, so opening prices rebounded step by step. As a result, this month ended down. April down only 7.5 hundredths of a cent. May down 1.5 cents. June down 1.25 cents. July down 1.75 cents. August down 2.75 cents.

After the wheat market opened in the morning, prices for all months fell uniformly. Imported wheat prices declined. When the market opened, the seriousness of the international situation had eased, and imported wheat was also reported down. Therefore, when prices opened, near-term months such as March and April fell only one or two cents due to actual demand. Distant-term months such as July and August fell sharply because industry players were hedging and bulls were actively exiting positions. The market dropped by a significant six or seven cents. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading in various months was slightly less active, and prices showed a slight upward trend. The flour market stabilized and there were rumors of a tax increase on imported wheat, so prices rebounded by one or two cents. As a result, the current month remained unchanged. July and August were down slightly four cents. The spot wheat market was flat and weak due to the free arrival of imported wheat. Anhui Bengbu wheat opened at 3.63 yuan. Shandong wheat opened at 3.66 yuan, totaling two thousand bags, by a new method.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Abundant Harvest of Sichuan Pickled Mustard Tuber 215

Recently, the new harvest of Sichuan pickled mustard tuber in the producing areas has greatly impacted the market. Prices have fallen repeatedly, and those in this business are suffering losses. It is estimated that the remaining stock from last year totals over ten thousand pieces. Less than half have been sold to date. Ordinary goods have reached 11-12 yuan. The worst ones are around 10 yuan, high quality 14 yuan. Because the new goods are not cleared out of the old stock, people are watching and not daring to stock up too much. However, the high-quality goods once reached 600 pieces and opened two or three hundred trading, selling at 22 yuan, and the current market is at 10 yuan. Both merchants and traders, in view of the excessive ups and downs in the past, have reportedly formed cooperative companies to work together for mutual benefit.

Silk and Tea: Financial Stagnation Leads to Sluggish Tea Industry 216

Tea is a major international trade commodity and a source of rural economic vitality. However, the extreme financial tightness in Shanghai has had a major impact on the tea industry. Besides the tea industry's economic organization and its own funds, it needs at least ten million yuan or more in credit from money shops each year. In recent years, tea firms have maintained their credit with money shops, but money shops are extremely tight due to the financial crunch, making it difficult for tea firms to meet the funding needs of tea producing regions. A certain tea firm, which has been operating for many years, has announced its closure because its money shop failed to provide financing. Many tea manufacturers in the inland regions have also been unable to continue operating for this reason. According to comprehensive reports, the production of black and green tea this year is expected to decrease by 200,000 boxes. Chinese tea exports are declining not because of obstruction in foreign sales, but because of the large decrease in production due to financial stagnation. This is regrettable.

Metals: Scattered Transactions in Deformed Steel Bars 217

Recently, there has been little buying and selling of 40-foot-long deformed steel bars by factories and construction gangs. Export business has also been limited due to the urgent need for funds. Therefore, the market is sluggish. Considering the poor environment, the price trend is likely to decline further. Currently, popular sizes such as 3-fen and 7-fen sell for only 107-8 yuan per ton, while 5-fen sizes sell for only 98-9 yuan. Other common sizes are reportedly priced around 103-4 yuan, down two to three yuan to five or six yuan compared to last week. As new shipments arrive frequently and sentiment is very weak, it is difficult to be optimistic about future market conditions. Therefore, those in this business are quite pessimistic. It is reported that yesterday's transactions were only 30-40 tons, which was purchased by the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau.

Free Talk

"Inertial Listlessness" 218

—Meng Jia

"Inertial listlessness" is not "our" ailment.

Like the "snake" characters in Gorky's "Song of the Falcon," who are content with the damp, warm, and dark burrows that he vehemently ridiculed, their "inactivity" is precisely because they fundamentally do not need to do anything. They drink fatty and greasy soup, take afternoon naps, and snore while sleeping; when they are in a good mood, they stroll with their wives or the like, wander around the park, attend banquets, and when they are tired of playing and lose interest, they stretch and exclaim, "How boring!" Oblomov's "longing to go far away" is nothing more than this kind of mentality. Moreover, as he himself acknowledged, the world does not need reforming, which is tantamount to saying that the world is too perfect? If people therefore believe that he really wants to "go far away," and that he does it "for humanity," then not only will Oblomov be laughed at as a fool, but we ourselves will also become fools. You think, with such a precious fellow who doesn't want to get married for fear of trouble, and is even too lazy to move house, can he really "go far away"?

The reason why Oblomov is like a docile pigeon, tucking his head under his wings, ready to spend his life under the same roof, is that this pigeon has too much food, so he wants to "retire to the forest" and hide in a warm nest doing comfortable things. If he had been starving long ago, or could not worry about tomorrow's food, even if he had memorized Yuan Zhonglang well, it would be difficult to have such great "elegance."

Turning the topic around, if "Mr. Luo" were alive now, he probably would not be so "hard-iron and taciturn," and silly. In his time, there were few things that could arouse abnormal excitement. There were no handball courts, no grand restaurants with naked dancers like Nora after she left home suspended above for the enjoyment of the guests, no dance halls with dance tickets and refreshments offered for one yuan and five cents, no "thrilling" soccer games with tickets costing five yuan. He was always curled up in his villa, eating, sleeping, eating, sleeping, always the same routine, and so "Mr. Luo" became "listless" and "melancholy." Alas, he was not born at the right time!

The Oblomovs of today are much smarter than before. Even if this is the laughter before death, they still want to enjoy it, and the ways of having fun are constantly emerging. "Inactivity as activity" makes them forget loneliness, and they even solemnly believe that they are "active" people.

"Inertial listlessness" is Daiyu or Baoyu's "idle sickness." And such a sickness seems to be a bit of the past. "Active listlessness," on the other hand, seems to be increasing and becoming more severe every day.

As for those who do not want to be "snakes" but cannot be "eagles," it is simply not "listlessness," but inexplicable "melancholy," although among them there are only a few who try to pretend to have a comfortable face—nothing more than "affectation."

After Dinner 219

—Lin Bin

Stepping out of the stinky little restaurant, feeling in my pocket: two dimes and a dozen or so copper coins. I don't have to worry about tomorrow's meal money!

Walking towards home (if you can call it that!), walking on the muddy slurry of the post-rain cobblestone road, feeling much more relaxed…

Suddenly, a thought flashed across my mind, catching a glimpse of the second landlord's opium face, and then a broken gong-like voice: "Rent! Overdue for a week!" The fleshy legs were like dragging chains, heavy.

—How to reply? … Oh, let's beat around the bush first! How to reply? …

Turning the corner: a burst of exotic fragrance, my head bumped into the shoulder of someone holding another person's arm, bounced back, and I saw: a college student!

"Don't you have eyes!" The eyes of the person with eyes were like sharp knives. The other person said: "Hmph!"

I returned a glance, meaning: What's so great! I'm a college graduate too, and I also have a lover, maybe even better than yours, although your crisp suit is more beautiful than my dirty cloth robe right now. Turning another corner: a cigarette and paper shop.

A worker took out three copper coins from his short pocket and threw them on the counter: "Two Company Brands."

My stomach itched, like worms crawling.

I slowed down my steps, felt in my robe pocket for three minutes, and finally took out three copper coins, like that worker, and threw them on the counter: "Two Company Brands…" But facing outwards, burning hot.

I put one in the corner of my mouth, lit it with the coil incense on the counter of another cigarette and paper shop, with a very arrogant air, telling the eyes钉着watching me in the counter: "This is not a Company Brand, it's a Big Beauty," but the heat on my face had not completely subsided.

My head was like a beehive, with countless bees buzzing: rent, how to reply…!

Walking, aimlessly walking…

My heart jumped, because:

Below the sidewalk, in the muddy slurry, a person was rolling around, no, a rare monster in the world: only the upper half of the legs were left, the ends wrapped in coarse burlap, and the burlap wrapped in muddy slurry. On the body, there were some rags, and in some places it looked like meat, it was unclear where the rags were and where the meat was, only muddy slurry. The face looked like it had just been dug out of a coal pile: no eyebrows, no eyelashes, only a pair of yellowish eyes, like a dying person, still radiating the last light of life. The corners of the mouth were almost pulled to the ears, with a mouth of yellow, smeared teeth. Shouting, raw shouting: "Sir! Madam! Do a good deed…"

A shiny car shot past like an arrow, splashing a burst of mud, splattering on the head, body, hands, and legs covered in mud, splattering on the yellowish pupils that were not covered in mud, wiping the mud on the pupils with a muddy hand.

Thinking: Why doesn't this kind of person roll into the Huangpu River? Why stay in the world to suffer such a living hell?…

On second thought: I was wrong. A black thread appeared before my eyes, one end holding his soul and the other end holding my soul.

——What about me? Yes, my legs are intact. I'm not lying rolling in the muddy slurry. I'm not shouting sir and madam on the street. But is it really different? No, the same, the essence of life is the same. The difference lies in the manner, in the degree.

I gritted my teeth and thought of everything…

"Hey, what are you doing standing here?"

My shoulder was patted, I turned my head: the great editor of the great magazine.

"Um."

"How's life been lately?"

"Um."

Seeing that he was about to leave, an invisible and powerful hand desperately squeezed words out of my throat:

"How's that manuscript I sent you a couple of weeks ago, Mr. ×? Please take a look as soon as possible… Help me out… I'm sorry… I can't help it…"

The editor nodded, smiled, and walked away, his mouth making no sound, but another mouth made a sound, the mouth of the "monster":

"Sir, Madam, do a good deed!"

Dying Lantern 220

—Da Bao

Bless the livestock to grow tall and strong,

Bless the wheat fields to have a good harvest…

With hope,

In the New Year, the villagers happily light lanterns in various locations,

The lantern light shines on the ancient lanes,

Decorated like a rosy village.

Like the ease with which hope dissipates,

The prosperous days slipped away;

Counting the New Year's expenses,

With worry—but pretending to have a lucky expression,

To the entrance of the lane, gathering the villagers for the "Dying Lantern" parade.

Carrying paper lanterns, only letting the gongs and drums bang and fill the world,

But no one can afford a string of firecrackers,

All the gorgeous clothes have been taken to the pawnshop,

Today we can only be ragged and tattered,

Like a team of miserable hungry people,

Asking the gods for help.

Qi Jin 221

—Chen Fuxi

"Mom, the classmates are saying again that I'm the son of a servant…"

"Let them say it."

A thick shadow lay on the mother's face.

Qi Jin was the son of Aunt Bao. Aunt Bao, as everyone knows, was a servant in the Zhang Mansion. Qi Jin lived with his mother in the mansion, and went to the nearby elementary school during the day.

There were many classmates at school, but everyone was prettier than Qi Jin. Qi Jin was a country bumpkin, with a dark face, worn-out, coarse cloth clothes, inarticulate, and not lively. From the moment he entered the school until now, he had been dull-witted all day long. The city kids could kick footballs, play with shuttlecocks, climb slides, jump ropes, and swing, but Qi Jin, as a newcomer to school, couldn't do any of these things. He was very lonely, and none of the classmates paid attention to him, and no one wanted to play with him. In the countryside, Qi Jin had many companions, riding on the backs of cows with them, throwing stones, or barefoot, running to the fields to find snails and catch green frogs, playing extraordinarily well; but once he arrived in the city, these things, for Qi Jin, were even unimaginable, and his attitude became so sluggish, walking slowly, almost trampling the ants on the ground to death. He was timid, cowardly, and when people deliberately scolded him or hit him, he didn't dare to resist, willing to suffer losses himself. However, city kids were very mischievous, and sometimes, some who were older than him, seeing Qi Jin, often intentionally brushed his shoulders or hit his head, and Qi Jin not only didn't hit back, but wouldn't even utter a word.

"Look at this countryman!…"

They shouted behind him. Shouting vigorously, they even threw stones at him. At school, he was truly an outcast, and no one was subjected to such bullying and humiliation as he was. It was as if his status was low, and the classmates who knew him were also unwilling to get close to him, as if being friendly with Qi Jin would make them lose face. Children have children's thoughts, and that kind of contemptuous, arrogant, and hypocritical thinking often exists even in innocent children, which is of course due to the poison given by the current society. They looked down on Qi Jin, which was pride, which was looking down on people. One day, a classmate lost a white copper ink box, and couldn't find it anywhere, so the classmates falsely accused Qi Jin of stealing it.

"You stole the ink box!"

"The ink box must have been stolen by the countryman!"

"I didn't steal it, I didn't…" Qi Jin said.

Qi Jin, surrounded by many classmates, was embarrassed. Everyone in the classroom said he stole it, one sentence from you, one sentence from me, and Qi Jin at this time didn't know how to argue. The next day, someone, no one knows who, found the stolen ink box in Qi Jin's book bag. When they pulled the ink box out of his book bag, everyone in the class laughed at him, saying he was a thief; saying his mother was a servant; saying he wore clothes, not knowing where he got them; saying he… such venomous, unsympathetic cold, he heard it, wanted to cry several times, but again tried his best to suppress it. He thought: did he really become a thief? How could the ink box be found in his book bag? But he also thought that he had indeed not stolen it. When he came out of the mansion in the morning, there was no ink box in his book bag! Then where did the ink box now found in his book bag come from? Could it have flown from the sky? He was young, honest by nature, and truly bewildered by this unwarranted slander. In the classroom, amidst the mockery, Qi Jin sat on the stool, his face blushing, not speaking, his head only felt a wave of dizziness.

"Everyone look at this little thief!"

When school was over and he was walking on the road, the classmates were still shouting loudly. But Qi Jin remained silent, as if admitting it. He lowered his head, looking at the ground, walking step by step, not daring to glance sideways at the roadside. When he walked back to Zhang Mansion, his heart trembled especially.

"Mom, the classmates are saying again that I'm…"

"Let them say it, Qi Jin."

However, Qi Jin, standing in front of his mother at this time, couldn't help but cry. Two lines of bright hot tears hung on his dark, thin face.

Viewing Plum Blossoms at Yoshino 222

— Zhao Qi

(Part Two)

Having passed through the small green-lacquered fence, I looked toward the gate adorned with the three characters "Rakurakuen" (Pleasure Garden) formed by plum blossoms, expecting it to be as noisy as the Meiyuan Garden in Wuxi, with hawkers, miscellaneous vendors, and rickshaw pullers. Contrary to my expectation, this preconceived notion was completely shattered, and I felt that it was purely a poetic realm. As I was about to enter the gate, beside the entrance was a wreath made of old plum branches, topped with a newly designed umbrella. Here stood a very beautiful young woman who personally pinned a paper plum blossom on the lapel of every visitor, regardless of age or gender, and presented a small package tied with colored string. Inside were a map showing the route, ferry tickets, candies that children loved, and a few refreshing pills. On her short sleeve was a red cloth with the words "Guidance" written on it, indicating that she was a guide dispatched by the Yoshino residents who welcomed tourists.

Entering the garden gate, I realized that it was not a garden, but a mountainside slope. We followed the winding path downwards, and in front of each household, high and low, there was a flower stand displaying various potted plants, marked with prices ranging from a few yuan to tens of cents. Below, a clear stream flowed, its gurgling sound resembling琴 music. I found a red line on the guidance map, which was the one called the奥多摩 River. After crossing the river, we walked up a dense pine path. The signpost pointed to the left, indicating the Yoshino plum blossom area. Standing there for a moment, I looked out into the distance. The area was surrounded by light green screens, with a pile of transparent cotton-like bodies in the middle, resembling shaved ice in a light blue glass bowl. This was because it was all white plum blossoms without any other varieties.

After walking a few steps, we entered a deep and winding plum blossom alley. The young ladies from the city, at this time, had taken off their coats, revealing their powder-covered necks and backs embroidered with flowers and birds, perfectly complementing the pure white blossoms, creating a sense of harmonious color and a unique oriental beauty.

The plum blossom area is over ten 里 (li, a Chinese unit of distance) in circumference. It is originally a large plum village, and the thatched houses of each household are hidden among the plum blossoms. The most flourishing places are the Meio-ken (Plum Oriole Pavilion) and the Keikei-en (Plum Brook Garden). We first passed by the Meio-ken, wandered around, and sat down on a cushion under the eaves of a house. I ordered a tempura (a Japanese dish), and the waitress was several times more respectful than those in the city. However, in the end, the price of even one fish was several times higher than in the city. The Japanese all brought their own lunch boxes because they knew this.

The sun was quietly setting, and we set off for the Keikei-en again. I felt that the branches of the plum trees were the most beautiful here. The wrinkled and reclining branches were all suitable for the composition of a painting. Sure enough, along the stream, I saw many stone tablets leaning against the pavilions, engraved with the years and inscriptions by xxxx painters and poets. As we walked further, we happened to meet those elderly scholars from the same train, sitting cross-legged under a cluster of flowers, with two lightly made-up young ladies pouring wine and grinding ink for them.

After we finished taking some pictures here, the sun had moved the shadow of the plum blossoms from the water surface to the opposite bank. I heard people say that it was only one and a half 里 (li) from here to 青梅 Station, so we decided to take the train at 青梅 Station.

Before leaving, what made me wonder was that there were various wooden signs to guide tourists, but why was there no sign saying "No Picking Flowers"? Perhaps the manager had overlooked this in his considerations!

Arriving at 青梅 Station, I sat down tiredly. Similarly, there was a young woman standing in that kind of flower wreath. The bright red afterglow shone on her smiling face, and her slender shadow stretched out as she offered a cup of tea to each of us and said a gentle word of comfort.

At 4:50, the train arrived. Most of the people in the carriage were returning from the plum grove. Seeing that even the children's clothes had nothing but a paper plum blossom pinned on them, I felt a deep shock in my heart. When people were thrown about by the train to the point of drooping their heads, I dared to quietly take off the flower I had picked from the plum grove and pinned on my hat, and dropped it out of the window.

March 10th, in Tokyo

Miscellaneous War Notes (10) (1) 223

— By Tokunaga Sunao, translated by Ye Yin

One-handed Xiong, not only had only one hand, but was also a cripple. At night, he would often spread out empty straw sacks on the dirt floor without flooring in my house and sleep with my dog named "Ba." Without bedding or anything else, he would take a half-piece of red felt, suitably place it on his head, and hug "Ba" to sleep. This had become his habit.

During the day, he would go to other people's houses to do odd jobs or help patients buy things, earning some money to buy "leftover food." When he earned a little more money, he would immediately start drinking. At that time, he, who was usually silent and taciturn, would become boisterous and garrulous.

His face protruded with huge cheekbones. When he smiled, many very large wrinkles would appear on his forehead and mouth.

Whenever the children saw Xiong going out to buy things with a medicine bottle, they would often come up and shout loudly:

"Lame Xiong, what time is it now..."

At this time, the wrinkles would appear on Xiong's face, and he would answer:

"Fifteen o'clock."

At the same time, he would make funny faces and dance for people to watch.
